	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Timeline of the John F. Kennedy assassination</h1>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_F._Kennedy_motorcade,_Dallas_crop.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png/220px-John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png/330px-John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png/440px-John_F._Kennedy_motorcade%2C_Dallas_crop.png 2x" data-file-width="3641" data-file-height="2444" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_F._Kennedy_motorcade,_Dallas_crop.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">United States President</a> <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Kennedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Jackie Kennedy">Mrs. Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Texas Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Connally" title="John Connally">John Connally</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Connally" title="Nellie Connally">Mrs. Connally</a>  minutes before the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">assassination</a></div></div></div>
<p>This article considers the detailed timeline of events before, during, and after the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">assassination of John F. Kennedy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of the United States">35th</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="box-sizing:border-box;width:100%;font-size:95%;padding:4px;border:none;border:1px #aaa solid"><div style="font-size:100%;line-height:1.6;font-weight:bold;background:transparent;text-align:left;;text-align:center">November 22, 1963</div><div class="mw-collapsible-content" style="background:transparent;text-align:left;;">
<p><b>10:40&#160;a.m. CST</b>: In <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth,_Texas" title="Fort Worth, Texas">Fort Worth, Texas</a>, Kennedy's motorcade departs <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Texas" title="Hotel Texas">Hotel Texas</a> for <a href="/wiki/Carswell_Air_Force_Base" title="Carswell Air Force Base">Carswell Air Force Base</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-www.jfk.org_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.jfk.org-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>11:20&#160;a.m. CST</b>: <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_One" title="Air Force One">Air Force One</a> departs Carswell Air Force Base for <a href="/wiki/Dallas,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas, Texas">Dallas, Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-www.jfk.org_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.jfk.org-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>11:35&#160;a.m. CST</b>: <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_Two" title="Air Force Two">Air Force Two</a> arrives at <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Love_Field" title="Dallas Love Field">Love Field</a> in Dallas.<sup id="cite_ref-www.jfk.org_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.jfk.org-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>11:38&#160;a.m. CST</b>: Air Force One arrives at <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Love_Field" title="Dallas Love Field">Love Field</a> in Dallas.<sup id="cite_ref-www.jfk.org_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.jfk.org-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>11:44&#160;a.m. CST</b>: The Kennedys and Connallys disembark <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_One" title="Air Force One">Air Force One</a> and are greeted by the Johnsons.<sup id="cite_ref-www.jfk.org_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.jfk.org-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>11:55&#160;a.m. CST</b>: The <a href="/wiki/Motorcade" title="Motorcade">motorcade</a> leaves <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Love_Field" title="Dallas Love Field">Love Field</a> for its 10-mile trip through downtown Dallas.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>12:30&#160;p.m. CST</b>: Shots are fired as the motorcade passes the <a href="/wiki/Texas_School_Book_Depository" title="Texas School Book Depository">Texas School Book Depository</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>12:34&#160;p.m. CST</b>: The first <a href="/wiki/United_Press_International" title="United Press International">United Press International</a> bulletin clears the wire stating: "Three shots were fired today at the president's motorcade in downtown Dallas."<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>12:36&#160;p.m. CST</b>: President Kennedy's <a href="/wiki/Limousine" title="Limousine">limousine</a> arrives at <a href="/wiki/Parkland_Memorial_Hospital" title="Parkland Memorial Hospital">Parkland Memorial Hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>12:40&#160;p.m. CST</b>: Viewers of the live soap opera <i><a href="/wiki/As_The_World_Turns" class="mw-redirect" title="As The World Turns">As The World Turns</a></i> receive the first national television report of the shooting from <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> News anchorman <a href="/wiki/Walter_Cronkite" title="Walter Cronkite">Walter Cronkite</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>12:45&#160;p.m. CST</b>: <a href="/wiki/Dan_Rather" title="Dan Rather">Dan Rather</a> of CBS calls <a href="/wiki/Parkland_Memorial_Hospital" title="Parkland Memorial Hospital">Parkland Memorial Hospital</a>; a doctor there tells him he believes Kennedy is dead.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>12:50&#160;p.m. CST</b>: Kennedy's top military aide General <a href="/wiki/Godfrey_McHugh" title="Godfrey McHugh">Godfrey McHugh</a> calls Air Force One from Parkland to state that they will soon be leaving for <a href="/wiki/Andrews_Air_Force_Base" title="Andrews Air Force Base">Andrews Air Force Base</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Esquire;_September_16,_2013_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Esquire;_September_16,_2013-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>1:00&#160;p.m. CST</b>: President Kennedy is officially pronounced dead.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>1:16&#160;p.m. CST</b>: The first report that Dallas Police Officer <a href="/wiki/J.D._Tippit" class="mw-redirect" title="J.D. Tippit">J.D. Tippit</a> has been shot.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>1:26&#160;p.m. CST</b>: <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_Johnson" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyndon Johnson">Lyndon Johnson</a> departs <a href="/wiki/Parkland_Memorial_Hospital" title="Parkland Memorial Hospital">Parkland Memorial Hospital</a> for <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Love_Field" title="Dallas Love Field">Love Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>1:30&#160;p.m. CST</b>: Johnson, protected by <a href="/wiki/Rufus_Youngblood" title="Rufus Youngblood">Rufus Youngblood</a> in a car driven by <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Curry" title="Jesse Curry">Jesse Curry</a>, along with passengers Congressmen <a href="/wiki/Albert_Richard_Thomas" title="Albert Richard Thomas">Albert Thomas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Homer_Thornberry" title="Homer Thornberry">Homer Thornberry</a>, arrives at Air Force One.<sup id="cite_ref-Esquire;_September_16,_2013_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Esquire;_September_16,_2013-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lady_Bird_Johnson" title="Lady Bird Johnson">Lady Bird Johnson</a>, Congressman <a href="/wiki/Jack_Brooks_(American_politician)" title="Jack Brooks (American politician)">Jack Brooks</a>, and three members of the Secret Service also arrive in a second car, and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Valenti" title="Jack Valenti">Jack Valenti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lem_Johns" title="Lem Johns">Lem Johns</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cliff_Carter_(Vice_Presidential_aide)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cliff Carter (Vice Presidential aide) (page does not exist)">Cliff Carter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Stoughton" class="mw-redirect" title="Cecil Stoughton">Cecil Stoughton</a> arrive in a third.<sup id="cite_ref-Esquire;_September_16,_2013_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Esquire;_September_16,_2013-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> They are followed by additional cars containing officials and aids for both Kennedy and Johnson.<sup id="cite_ref-Esquire;_September_16,_2013_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Esquire;_September_16,_2013-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>1:33&#160;p.m. CST</b>: White House Assistant Press Secretary <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Kilduff" title="Malcolm Kilduff">Malcolm Kilduff</a> announces at Parkland Memorial Hospital that Kennedy is dead.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Esquire;_September_16,_2013_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Esquire;_September_16,_2013-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>1:38&#160;p.m. CST</b>: CBS News anchor Cronkite reports the official word that President Kennedy is dead and Johnson will be sworn in as the United States' 36th President.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Esquire;_September_16,_2013_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Esquire;_September_16,_2013-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>1:40&#160;p.m. CST</b>: Johnson telephones <a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_General" title="United States Attorney General">Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a> to express his condolences and ask where he should take the <a href="/wiki/Oath_of_office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States" title="Oath of office of the President of the United States">oath of office of the President of the United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Esquire;_September_16,_2013_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Esquire;_September_16,_2013-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>1:50&#160;p.m. CST</b>: Johnson telephones his friend <a href="/wiki/Irving_Loeb_Goldberg" title="Irving Loeb Goldberg">Irving Goldberg</a>, an attorney.<sup id="cite_ref-Esquire;_September_16,_2013_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Esquire;_September_16,_2013-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The two decide to ask <a href="/wiki/Sarah_T._Hughes" title="Sarah T. Hughes">Sarah T. Hughes</a> to administer the oath.<sup id="cite_ref-Esquire;_September_16,_2013_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Esquire;_September_16,_2013-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>1:51&#160;p.m. CST</b>: <a href="/wiki/Lee_Harvey_Oswald" title="Lee Harvey Oswald">Lee Harvey Oswald</a> is arrested at the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Theater" class="mw-redirect" title="Texas Theater">Texas Theater</a> in Dallas.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>2:10&#160;p.m. CST</b>: <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Zapruder" title="Abraham Zapruder">Abraham Zapruder</a> arrives at <a href="/wiki/WFAA-TV" class="mw-redirect" title="WFAA-TV">WFAA-TV</a> in Dallas and is interviewed about his film of the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>2:13&#160;p.m. CST</b>: Police find the weapon used to kill the president on the 6th floor of the Texas School Book depository.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>2:38&#160;p.m. CST</b>: Johnson is sworn in as President by federal judge <a href="/wiki/Sarah_T._Hughes" title="Sarah T. Hughes">Sarah Hughes</a> on Air Force One.<sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>2:46&#160;p.m. CST</b>: Air Force One departs Love Field for <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a><sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prelude">Prelude</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Prelude">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>October 24, 1956:</b> <a href="/wiki/Lee_Harvey_Oswald" title="Lee Harvey Oswald">Lee Harvey Oswald</a> drops out of <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">high school</a> and joins the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">U.S. Marine Corps</a>, where he is trained as a sharpshooter.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p><b>October 31, 1959:</b> Oswald goes to the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, and is sent to work at an electronics factory in <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>. 
</p><p><b>November 8, 1960:</b> <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> wins the <a href="/wiki/1960_United_States_presidential_election" title="1960 United States presidential election">1960 United States presidential election</a>. 
</p><p><b>June 13, 1962:</b> Oswald returns to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> with his wife <a href="/wiki/Marina_Oswald_Porter" title="Marina Oswald Porter">Marina</a> and their child to live in <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 6, 1962:</b> <a href="/wiki/John_Connally" title="John Connally">John Connally</a> (D) is <a href="/wiki/1962_Texas_gubernatorial_election" title="1962 Texas gubernatorial election">elected</a> <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Governor of Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>January 15, 1963:</b> Connally is sworn in as Governor of Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> As the Governor of Texas he will help plan and serve as host for President Kennedy's trip to Texas.
</p><p><b>February 22, 1963:</b> <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Paine" title="Ruth Paine">Ruth Paine</a> meets the Oswalds at a party given at Everett Glover's house.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>March 12, 1963:</b> An order for a rifle with a mounted scope is sent to Klein's Sporting Goods from someone named "A. Hidell" (an alias used by Oswald) to be delivered to a P.O. Box that was rented by Oswald.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>March 13, 1963:</b> Order received by Klein's Sporting Goods from A. Hidell P.O. Box 2915 Dallas, TX
for an Italian Carbine 6.5 W/4X Scope. Total cost is $21.45 for rifle with serial number C2766.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>March 17, 1963:</b> Marina Oswald sends a letter to the Russian Embassy in Washington DC asking to be granted an entrance visa to the USSR.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oswald is given notice in the latter part of March that he will be terminated from his job.
</p><p><b>April 6, 1963:</b> Oswald works his last day at Jaggars-Chiles-Stovall.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>April 10, 1963:</b> Someone fires a bullet that just misses retired General <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Walker" title="Edwin Walker">Edwin Walker</a>, an advocate of <a href="/wiki/Far-right_politics_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Far-right politics in the United States">far right politics</a> and strongly <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">anti-communist</a>. The police determine the shot came from a distance of less than 40 yards.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The case remained unsolved until two weeks after the death of Lee Oswald when Marina Oswald admitted to the FBI it may have been her husband who fired the shot.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>April 11, 1963:</b> U.S. Rep. <a href="/wiki/Albert_Richard_Thomas" title="Albert Richard Thomas">Albert Richard Thomas</a> (D-Tex) announces his retirement from Congress due to health reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>April 23, 1963:</b> <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President</a> <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a>, a Texas native, tells reporters in <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a> that President Kennedy may visit Texas sometime that summer. LBJ hopes Kennedy's schedule would allow him to have a breakfast in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Worth">Fort Worth</a>, a luncheon in Dallas, an afternoon tea in <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio" title="San Antonio">San Antonio</a> and dinner in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>June 5, 1963:</b> President Kennedy, Vice President Johnson, and Governor Connally were together in a meeting in <a href="/wiki/El_Paso,_Texas" title="El Paso, Texas">El Paso</a> when they agree to a second presidential visit to the state of Texas later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-WarrenCommission-Page28_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WarrenCommission-Page28-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> (In 1978 Connally testified to the <a href="/wiki/House_Select_Committee_on_Assassinations" class="mw-redirect" title="House Select Committee on Assassinations">House Select Committee on Assassinations</a> that in the spring of 1962 "Vice President Johnson told me then that President Kennedy wanted to come to Texas, he wanted to come to Texas to raise some money, have some fund-raising affairs over the State.")
</p><p><b>June 6, 1963:</b> Rep. Albert Thomas announces he is reconsidering his decision to retire and may still run again for reelection<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> based on the advice of Vice President Lyndon Johnson.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kennedy later decided to embark on the trip with three basic goals in mind: he wanted to help raise more <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> presidential campaign fund contributions;<sup id="cite_ref-WarrenCommission-Page28_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WarrenCommission-Page28-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> he wanted to begin his quest for reelection in November 1964;<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and, because the Kennedy-Johnson ticket had barely won Texas in 1960 (and had even lost in Dallas), President Kennedy wanted to help mend political fences among several leading Texas Democratic party members who appeared to be fighting politically amongst themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-VisitPlanned_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VisitPlanned-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>June 24, 1963:</b> Oswald applies for a US passport in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> stating he intended to depart from New Orleans during the period from October to December 1963 for proposed travel as a tourist for 3 months to one year's duration. The next day he was issued US Passport DO 92526 which was valid for three years to all countries except <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Socialist_Republic_of_Albania" title="People&#39;s Socialist Republic of Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and those portions of <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">Vietnam</a> that were under communist control.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>September 17, 1963:</b> <a href="/wiki/Jack_Valenti" title="Jack Valenti">Jack Valenti</a> sends an invitation to the <a href="/wiki/White_House_Office" title="White House Office">White House</a> asking if President Kennedy would attend an Appreciation Dinner in Houston on November 21, 1963 honoring Albert Thomas for his decision not to retire from Congress. The invitation is received at the White House on September 19, 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lee Oswald is issued a 15 day Mexican tourist card using the name LEE, Harvey Oswald.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>September 20, 1963:</b> President Kennedy addresses the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">General Assembly</a> and offers the Soviet Union a joint expedition to the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The proposal is controversial with many members of Congress and raises fresh questions about how much money should be appropriated to the <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> budget.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>September 21, 1963:</b> Rep. Albert Thomas (D-Tex), a member of the powerful <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_Committee_on_Appropriations" title="United States House Committee on Appropriations">House Appropriations Committee</a> and Chairman of its Subcommittee of Independent Offices that was reviewing the Kennedy Administration's record $5.3 billion 1964 <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> budget proposal,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> sends a letter to the President asking for clarification of his U.N. speech regarding a <a href="/wiki/Space_Race#Kennedy_proposes_a_joint_US-USSR_program" title="Space Race">joint Soviet-US moon landing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> He wonders if this proposal indicates a weakening of America's effort in the space program. Thomas had also played an instrumental role in the location of the Manned Spacecraft Center, now known as the <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Space_Center" title="Johnson Space Center">Johnson Space Center</a> in his home district of Houston, Texas.
</p><p><b>September 23, 1963:</b> President Kennedy responds to Congressman Albert Thomas letter requesting clarification of the goals of the U.S. Space Program by writing him a "Dear Al" letter explaining his position.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ruth Paine drives Marina Oswald from New Orleans back to her home in <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">Irving, Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Late that night Lee Oswald also leaves New Orleans<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> to travel to <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> in the hopes of somehow gaining entrance to Cuba<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> where travel has been banned from the United States.
</p><p><b>September 24–28, 1963:</b> President Kennedy embarks on an eleven-state conservation tour which include visits to <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>September 24, 1963:</b> At a press conference in <a href="/wiki/Austin" class="mw-redirect" title="Austin">Austin</a>, Texas, Governor Connally announces he will visit Washington DC from October 2–4, 1963 and he hopes to see the President but he has no plans to invite him to visit Texas but that he would be delighted if he came.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The decision is reached this evening by the White House to accept the invitation to the Albert Thomas dinner in Houston and turn it into a 2-day political trip encompassing all the major cities of Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-Baskin_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baskin-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
Although Kennedy had wanted to visit Texas at some point, he had not planned to go at this particular time.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> But because of the invitation to speak at the Appreciation Dinner in Houston for Albert Thomas on November 21, 1963, the President decided to time his visit to Texas around that event<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> instead of at some later date.
</p><p><b>September 25, 1963:</b> Late that evening White House sources, in an exclusive to the <i><a href="/wiki/Dallas_Morning_News" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas Morning News">Dallas Morning News</a></i>, announce that the President will visit Texas November 21–22, 1963 and it will include Dallas.<sup id="cite_ref-Baskin_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baskin-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>September 26, 1963:</b> The <i>Dallas Morning News</i> is the first newspaper that announces the visit to Texas by President Kennedy in an article covering the President's conservation tour in Jackson Hole, Wyoming.<sup id="cite_ref-Baskin_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baskin-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>September 27, 1963:</b> Lee Oswald arrives in Mexico City and registers at the Hotel del Comercio.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> He visits the Cuban Consulate three times in an attempt to secure a visa to Cuba and also the Soviet Embassy to obtain a visa from them but is denied in both instances.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>September 30, 1963:</b> Lee Oswald purchases a bus ticket using the alias Mr. H. O. Lee that leaves Mexico City for <a href="/wiki/Laredo,_Texas" title="Laredo, Texas">Laredo, Texas</a> at 0830 on October 2, 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 3, 1963:</b> Oswald arrives in Dallas and spends the night at the YMCA.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 4, 1963:</b> Governor Connally meets with President Kennedy at the White House.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oswald applies for a job at Padgett Printing but is not hired because of a poor recommendation by the owner of Jaggars-Chiles-Stovall.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Oswald returns to stay at the Paine's residence in Irving, Texas for the weekend.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 7, 1963:</b> <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Baker" title="Bobby Baker">Bobby Baker</a> resigns his position as Secretary to the <a href="/wiki/Party_leaders_of_the_United_States_Senate" title="Party leaders of the United States Senate">Senate Majority Leader</a> because of various scandals. He was appointed to the position by <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> in 1955 and was a close personal friend of his.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 10, 1963:</b> The House of Representatives voted 302–32 to pass the 1964 fiscal year Independent Offices Appropriations Bill which contained funding for NASA and 25 other independent government agencies. Guiding the bill through the House was the Chairman of the subcommittee Rep. Albert Thomas (D-Tex). The bill prohibited NASA from spending any of its budget on a joint Soviet Moon landing.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 11, 1963:</b> Kenneth O'Donnell sends a letter of reply to Jack Valenti formally accepting his invitation for the President to speak at the dinner honoring Rep. Albert Thomas.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 15, 1963:</b> Ruth Paine calls the <a href="/wiki/Texas_School_Book_Depository" title="Texas School Book Depository">Texas School Book Depository</a> and speaks to building superintendent Roy Truly, and convinces him to give Oswald a job interview. Truly interviews him that same day and hires Oswald as a temporary employee and he starts training the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 20, 1963:</b> <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_O%27Donnell" title="Kenneth O&#39;Donnell">Kenneth O'Donnell</a>, special assistant and Appointments Secretary to President Kennedy, calls Jerry Bruno the advance man for the Kennedy trips, and asks him to come to the White House to discuss the planning of the trip to Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 21, 1963:</b> Bruno meets with O'Donnell and is told to contact <a href="/wiki/Walter_Jenkins" title="Walter Jenkins">Walter Jenkins</a> one of Vice President Lyndon Johnson's top administrative assistants to get his input for the trip.
</p><p><b>October 24, 1963:</b> Bruno meets with <a href="/wiki/Walter_Jenkins" title="Walter Jenkins">Walter Jenkins</a> who tells Bruno the stops Governor Connally has suggested. First stop would be to fly to San Antonio on November 21 and motorcade to <a href="/wiki/Brooks_Air_Force_Base" title="Brooks Air Force Base">Brooks Air Force Base</a>, then fly to Houston and motorcade to the <a href="/wiki/Rice_Hotel" class="mw-redirect" title="Rice Hotel">Rice Hotel</a> where the Albert Thomas dinner was originally scheduled to take place that evening and stay overnight there. On the morning of November 22 fly to Fort Worth to receive an honorary degree at <a href="/wiki/Texas_Christian_University" title="Texas Christian University">Texas Christian University</a> (TCU) at 9:30 a.m., then from Fort Worth motorcade the short distance to Dallas<sup id="cite_ref-Bruno_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bruno-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> for a luncheon at the Statler Hilton Hotel for the annual meeting of the Dallas Citizens Council.<sup id="cite_ref-Bruno_23_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bruno_23-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and then finally a fundraising dinner in Austin. Jenkins suggested Bruno go to Texas, meet with Governor Connally and evaluate the sites himself and to also meet with Senator <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Yarborough" title="Ralph Yarborough">Ralph Yarborough</a> (D-Tex), who was a bitter political enemy of Connally and Johnson so as to avoid any trouble between the two parties on the trip.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>United States Ambassador to the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Adlai_Stevenson_II" title="Adlai Stevenson II">Adlai Stevenson II</a> gives a contentious speech on what is designated <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Day" title="United Nations Day">United Nations Day</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Kay_Bailey_Hutchison_Convention_Center" title="Kay Bailey Hutchison Convention Center">Dallas Memorial Auditorium</a> where he is booed and heckled. After the speech, as he is walking to his limo he stops to talk to a loud group of protesters when he is suddenly hit on the head with a picket sign and then spit upon.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 28, 1963:</b> Jerry Bruno flies to Austin, Texas to begin his evaluation of the stops being considered for the Kennedy visit on November 21–22.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 29, 1963:</b> Bruno meets with Henry Brown who is President of the Texas <a href="/wiki/AFL%E2%80%93CIO" title="AFL–CIO">AFL-CIO</a> and a friend of Senator <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Yarborough" title="Ralph Yarborough">Ralph Yarborough</a> to obtain his input from the labor leaders. He then has lunch with Governor Connally to review his itinerary, which includes an honorary degree from Texas Christian University, an event, because Kennedy is Catholic, that Bruno considers one of the highlights of the trip.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Connally informs Bruno that he has assigned different members of his staff to each stop on his itinerary and they would be in charge of the visit.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Bruno tells Connally that he welcomes his input and suggestions but the final decisions on where the President goes in Texas will be made by the White House.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Governor Connally announces that a "Texas welcome dinner" for President Kennedy will be held in Austin on November 22nd. The governor said the dinner will be a $100 per plate event held at 7:30 pm in Austin Municipal Auditorium as a climax to the President's trip to Texas. It is sponsored by the State Democratic Executive Committee. Besides the Albert Thomas Appreciation Dinner in Houston on November 21st, no other plans have been completed.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 30, 1963:</b> Bruno is flown to the various cities in Texas that the President would visit with Clifton Carter who is one of Vice-President Johnson's top aides.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The San Antonio and Houston sites are checked and confirmed as acceptable by Bruno but when visiting Texas Christian University in Fort Worth he is informed by school officials that TCU has no intention of conferring an honorary degree on the President. Only the use of their campus as a location for a speech was approved by the university. Bruno informs Gov. Connally of this development and Connally says he will meet with the University Board of Regents the next night.<sup id="cite_ref-Bruno_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bruno-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Bruno then travels to Dallas to evaluate the ballroom at the Statler Hilton Hotel where the luncheon was going to be held for the President on Friday November 22. He is met there by <a href="/wiki/J._Erik_Jonsson" title="J. Erik Jonsson">J. Erik Jonsson</a>, Chairman of the Citizen Council (and one of the owners of <a href="/wiki/Texas_Instruments" title="Texas Instruments">Texas Instruments</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Robert_B._Cullum" title="Robert B. Cullum">Robert B. Cullum</a> Chairman of the Dallas Chamber of Commerce and owner of the <a href="/wiki/Tom_Thumb_Food_Stores" class="mw-redirect" title="Tom Thumb Food Stores">Tom Thumb Food Stores</a>. Cullum informs Bruno that the ballroom at the Statler Hilton is now unavailable because members of a Bottler's convention being held the week of the President's visit had reserved it and would not give it up for the President.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Bruno now has to find another site for the luncheon. Jonsson and Cullum suggest the Dallas Trade Mart, but after visiting the site, Bruno doesn't like it because of the many catwalks that would be over the President. He feels that in light of the Stevenson incident which had just occurred a few days earlier the catwalks could present a security problem. He asks to be shown other available sites in Dallas.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>October 31, 1963</b>: Bruno visits two other potential luncheon sites, the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Memorial_Auditorium" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas Memorial Auditorium">Dallas Memorial Auditorium</a> which he deems too large, and the <a href="/wiki/Graduate_Research_Center_of_the_Southwest" class="mw-redirect" title="Graduate Research Center of the Southwest">Graduate Research Center of the Southwest</a> which he believes would be too far out of town and thus impractical. He is also informed that Governor Connally is unhappy with his decision not to go to the Trade Mart because of the catwalk issue. Bruno agrees to visit the Trade Mart again but afterward still has misgivings. Connally telephones that he has met with the TCU Board of Regents and they will not confer an honorary degree on the President.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Bruno is now faced with two holes in the schedule: Fort Worth and Dallas. One last place is suggested as a luncheon possibility, the Women's Building (now known as <a href="/wiki/The_Women%27s_Museum" title="The Women&#39;s Museum">The Women's Museum</a>) at the State Fairgrounds at Fair Park.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>President Kennedy is asked at a press conference about rumors that Lyndon Johnson will be dumped in 1964 as a running mate,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and  whether he still wanted Johnson on the ticket, and if he expects that he will be on the ticket? Kennedy responds yes, to both of the questions.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 1, 1963:</b> Bruno returns to Washington D.C. with the Dallas luncheon site location still undecided. The Fort Worth visit is resolved by having their Chamber of Commerce sponsor a breakfast for the President. Because of this, the President's overnight stay is changed from Houston to Fort Worth so he will have time to attend the breakfast.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 2, 1963:</b> The arrest and assassination of <a href="/wiki/Ngo_Dinh_Diem" title="Ngo Dinh Diem">Ngô Đình Diệm</a>, the president of <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">South Vietnam</a>, marked the culmination of a successful <a href="/wiki/CIA" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA">CIA</a>-backed <i><a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d&#39;état">coup d'état</a></i> led by General <a href="/wiki/D%C6%B0%C6%A1ng_V%C4%83n_Minh" title="Dương Văn Minh">Dương Văn Minh</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ng%C3%B4_%C4%90%C3%ACnh_Di%E1%BB%87m" class="mw-redirect" title="Ngô Đình Diệm">Diệm</a> and his adviser, his younger brother <a href="/wiki/Ng%C3%B4_%C4%90%C3%ACnh_Nhu" title="Ngô Đình Nhu">Ngô Đình Nhu</a>, were arrested after the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Republic_of_Vietnam" title="Army of the Republic of Vietnam">Army of the Republic of Vietnam</a> (ARVN) had been successful in a bloody overnight siege on <a href="/wiki/Gia_Long_Palace" title="Gia Long Palace">Gia Long Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City" title="Ho Chi Minh City">Saigon</a>. President Kennedy canceled his planned visit to Chicago to attend the Army-Air Force football game so he could instead keep in close touch with developments in South Vietnam.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p><b>November 3, 1963:</b> Vice President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> leaves Washington D.C. to fly to <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> for a one week visit of the <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a> countries.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 6, 1963:</b> White House Press Secretary <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Salinger" title="Pierre Salinger">Pierre Salinger</a> announces that <a href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Kennedy_Onassis" title="Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis">First Lady Jacqueline Kennedy</a> has decided to accompany the President on his trip to Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 7, 1963:</b> The Albert Thomas Appreciation Dinner being held on November 21, 1963 sells out a second time. Organizers of the dinner had already moved the venue from the Rice Hotel to the larger Sam Houston Coliseum because they could not accommodate the  increased demand for tickets once it became known that President Kennedy would attend. After it was announced that the First Lady would also be there, tickets to the dinner sold out again.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 8, 1963:</b> Bobby Baker is featured on the cover of <a href="/wiki/Life_(magazine)" title="Life (magazine)"><i>Life</i> magazine</a> with the headline “THE BOBBY BAKER BOMBSHELL, Capital Buzzes Over Stories of Misconduct in High Places”.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The article features a full page picture of Vice President Lyndon Johnson with his arm around Baker and reveals he was known around the Senate as “Lyndon’s boy”.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While Johnson was travelling abroad visiting the <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a> countries, Life Magazine’s Pulitzer Prize-winning reporter, William G. Lambert received approval from Managing Editor George P. Hunt to significantly expand his nine-member team who were investigating <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Baker" title="Bobby Baker">Bobby Baker</a> and send them to Texas to start focusing on the financial affairs of Lyndon Johnson. Teams of reporters began working in Johnson City, Austin, and the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Hill_Country" title="Texas Hill Country">Texas Hill Country</a> searching through deeds and other records of recent land sales and the real-estate and banking transactions of the Johnson family’s L.B.J. Company. Reporters were also digging into the advertising sales and other activities of <a href="/wiki/KTBC_(TV)" title="KTBC (TV)">KTBC (TV)</a>, the cornerstone of the Johnson's extensive radio and television interests. The first of what was supposed to be a series of articles laying out some of their new findings on LBJ was soon written by Keith Wheeler for future publication.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 15, 1963:</b> President Kennedy delivers a speech in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> at the <a href="/wiki/AFL-CIO" class="mw-redirect" title="AFL-CIO">AFL-CIO</a> convention then flies to <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">West Palm Beach, Florida</a> to spend his last weekend.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 16, 1963:</b> President Kennedy tours Cape Canaveral to inspect plans for the U.S. man-to-the-moon project and to direct the submarine firing of a Polaris A-2 missile.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 17, 1963:</b> President Kennedy stays in Palm Beach, Florida spending much of the day preparing for the five speeches he will deliver the next day in Tampa and Miami.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 18, 1963:</b> President Kennedy gives three speeches in Tampa plus a motorcade through the city, then flies to Miami and gives two more speeches including a hemisphere policy talk at the Miami Beach convention of the Inter-American Press Association where he urges the Cuban people to overthrow the Castro regime.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> He then flies back to Washington D.C. late that evening. On the return flight, Kennedy confided to his good friend Senator <a href="/wiki/George_Smathers" title="George Smathers">George Smathers</a> (D-FL) that Vice President Lyndon Johnson wanted First Lady Jacqueline Kennedy to ride in the car with him during the upcoming tour of Texas.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 19, 1963</b>: In an informal discussion with his secretary <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_Lincoln" title="Evelyn Lincoln">Evelyn Lincoln</a>, President Kennedy revealed some of the plans he had for his next administration if he were re-elected in 1964. He informs Lincoln that he is seriously considering replacing Vice President Lyndon Johnson as his running mate in 1964 with Governor <a href="/wiki/Terry_Sanford" title="Terry Sanford">Terry Sanford</a> of North Carolina.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>November 22, 1963:</b> The second in a series of articles on the Bobby Baker scandal appears in Life Magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kennedy's upcoming trip to Dallas was first announced to the public in September 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The exact motorcade route was finalized on November 18 and announced to the public a few days before November 22.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the third week of October 1963, Lee Harvey Oswald was living in a rented room in a boarding house in the <a href="/wiki/Oak_Cliff" title="Oak Cliff">Oak Cliff</a> district of Dallas. He had just been hired for a seasonal job at the <a href="/wiki/Texas_School_Book_Depository" title="Texas School Book Depository">Texas School Book Depository</a> as a $1.25/hour clerk, filling customer orders for books.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Oswald had obtained the job after a referral by Ruth Paine,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> with whom Lee's wife, Marina Oswald, and the Oswald children were living.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> At about the same time, Ruth had also separated from her husband, Michael Paine.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A month before Kennedy's ill-fated trip, U.N. Ambassador Stevenson was jeered, jostled, hit by a sign, and spat upon when he visited Dallas to mark <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Day" title="United Nations Day">U.N. Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Dallas Police were fearful that similar demonstrations would occur when Kennedy visited Dallas.<sup id="cite_ref-DeathNews_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeathNews-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Several people, including Stevenson, warned JFK against coming to Dallas, but Kennedy ignored their advice.<sup id="cite_ref-VisitPlanned_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VisitPlanned-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Dallas Police Chief Jesse Curry increased the level of security during Kennedy's visit; he put into effect the most stringent security precautions in the city's history.<sup id="cite_ref-DeathNews_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeathNews-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Curry even deputized citizens to take action for any suspicious acts that could have been pointed towards the president.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="President_Kennedy.27s_Texas_trip_schedule"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="President_Kennedy's_Texas_trip_schedule">President Kennedy's Texas trip schedule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: President Kennedy&#039;s Texas trip schedule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Thursday.2C_November_21"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Thursday,_November_21">Thursday, November 21</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Thursday, November 21">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dd><dl><dd><a href="/wiki/San_Antonio,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="San Antonio, Texas">San Antonio</a>: Dedication speech for U.S. Air Force School of Aerospace Medicine at <a href="/wiki/Brooks_Air_Force_Base" title="Brooks Air Force Base">Brooks Air Force Base</a>.</dd>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Houston, Texas">Houston</a>: Testimonial dinner at the <a href="/wiki/Sam_Houston_Coliseum" title="Sam Houston Coliseum">Sam Houston Coliseum</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> honoring Congressman <a href="/wiki/Albert_Richard_Thomas" title="Albert Richard Thomas">Albert Thomas</a>.</dd>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth,_Texas" title="Fort Worth, Texas">Fort Worth</a>: Arrival at <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Texas" title="Hotel Texas">Hotel Texas</a>.</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<h3><span id="Friday.2C_November_22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Friday,_November_22">Friday, November 22</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Friday, November 22">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>Fort Worth: <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_commerce" title="Chamber of commerce">Chamber of Commerce</a> breakfast speech at <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Texas" title="Hotel Texas">Hotel Texas</a>.</dd>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>: Luncheon speech attended by Dallas Citizens Council, Dallas Assembly and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Dallas" title="University of Texas at Dallas">Graduate Research Center of the Southwest</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Market_Center" title="Dallas Market Center">Trade Mart</a>.</dd>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin</a>: Fundraising dinner speech at Municipal Auditorium.</dd>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Johnson_City,_Texas" title="Johnson City, Texas">Johnson City</a>: Weekend of relaxation at <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_National_Historical_Park" title="Lyndon B. Johnson National Historical Park">Lyndon Johnson's ranch</a>.</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="November_21:_Arrival_in_Fort_Worth">November 21: Arrival in Fort Worth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: November 21: Arrival in Fort Worth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On Thursday, November 21, 1963, at 11:07&#160;p.m., <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_One" title="Air Force One">Air Force One</a> lands at <a href="/wiki/Carswell_Air_Force_Base" title="Carswell Air Force Base">Carswell Air Force Base</a> on the outskirts of Fort Worth, Texas. The president and his wife walk down the steps of the aircraft and are met by Raymond Buck, president of the Fort Worth Chamber of Commerce and his wife.
</p><p>Air Force Two also lands at Carswell with vice president Lyndon B. Johnson, the Texas governor John Connally, and Senator Ralph Yarborough. Connally and Yarborough dislike each other so much that Yarborough is unwilling to travel in the same car as Johnson, who is an ally of Connally. The following day, the president tells him to ride with Johnson.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At 11:35&#160;p.m., the First Couple arrives at the Hotel Texas in Fort Worth, after being cheered by thousands of well-wishers lined on the route towards the West Freeway, despite the late time and rainy weather.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="November_22:_Fort_Worth_breakfast_speech">November 22: Fort Worth breakfast speech</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: November 22: Fort Worth breakfast speech">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On Friday, November 22, 1963, at 8:45&#160;a.m., the president is speaking before breakfast in a square across Eighth Street, accompanied by Congressman Jim Wright, Senator Yarborough, Governor Connally and Vice President Johnson. Kennedy is praising Fort Worth's aviation industry.
</p><p>At 9:10&#160;a.m., JFK takes his place in the hotel's Grand Ballroom for the scheduled speech, the First Lady arriving amid loud applause 15 minutes later.
</p><p>After the speech, Roy Kellerman, the Secret Service agent in charge of the trip, is advised by Kenny O'Donnell that the presidential limousine should have its bubbletop off if it's not raining in Dallas.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later, press secretary Mac Kilduff shows the First Couple a disturbing advertisement seen in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dallas_Morning_News" title="The Dallas Morning News">The Dallas Morning News</a></i>, ironically and critically headlined 'Welcome Mr. Kennedy to Dallas'. JFK tells Jacqueline: 'We're heading into nut country today. […]'
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="November_22:_Arrival_in_Dallas">November 22: Arrival in Dallas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: November 22: Arrival in Dallas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On Friday, November 22, 1963, at 11:38&#160;a.m. <a href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone_(North_America)" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Time Zone (North America)">CST</a>, Kennedy, his wife <a href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Kennedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacqueline Kennedy">Jacqueline</a>, and the rest of the presidential entourage arrived at <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Love_Field" title="Dallas Love Field">Love Field</a> in northwest Dallas aboard <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_One" title="Air Force One">Air Force One</a> after a very short flight from nearby <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Joint_Reserve_Base_Fort_Worth" title="Naval Air Station Joint Reserve Base Fort Worth">Carswell Air Force Base</a>, west of Fort Worth.<sup id="cite_ref-www.jfk.org_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.jfk.org-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013_2-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here_and_Now;_November_22,_2013-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The motorcade cars had been lined up in a certain order earlier that morning. The original schedule was for the president to proceed in a long motorcade from <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Love_Field" title="Dallas Love Field">Love Field</a> through downtown Dallas, and end at the Dallas Business and Trade Mart.
</p><p>The motorcade was scheduled to enter <a href="/wiki/Dealey_Plaza" title="Dealey Plaza">Dealey Plaza</a> at 12:10&#160;p.m., followed by a 12:15&#160;p.m. arrival at the Trade Mart, where President Kennedy was scheduled to deliver a speech and share a steak luncheon with local government, business, religious, and civic leaders and their spouses. Invitations that were sent out specify a noon start time to the luncheon while SS agent Lawson told Chief Curry that after arriving at Love Field and leaving at 11:30 the 38- to 45-minute trip would get them to the Trade Mart on time. Air Force One touched down at 11:39&#160;a.m. and the Presidential motorcade did not leave Love Field until approximately fifteen minutes later.
</p><p>Dallas/Fort Worth's television stations were given separate assignments. As Bob Walker of <a href="/wiki/WFAA" title="WFAA">WFAA</a>-TV 8 (ABC) was providing live coverage of the President's arrival at Love Field, <a href="/wiki/KDFW" title="KDFW">KRLD-TV</a> 4 (CBS) with <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Barker" title="Eddie Barker">Eddie Barker</a> was set up at the Trade Mart for Kennedy's luncheon speech. <a href="/wiki/KTVT" title="KTVT">KTVT</a> Channel 11 (Independent), had originated live coverage of the President's breakfast speech in Fort Worth earlier that day. On hand to report the arrival on radio was Joe Long of <a href="/wiki/KLIF_(AM)" title="KLIF (AM)">KLIF</a> 1190.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorcade_vehicles_and_personnel">Motorcade vehicles and personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Motorcade vehicles and personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

Burkley (page does not exist)">George G. Burkley</a>, MD, the President's Physician), several extra cars, and police escorts follow.</li>
<li>Abbreviations used above include:
<ul><li>SA: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secret_Service" title="United States Secret Service">Secret Service</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secret_Service#Special_Agent" title="United States Secret Service">Special Agent</a></li>
<li>SAIC: Special Agent in Charge</li>
<li>ASAIC: Assistant Special Agent in Charge</li>
<li>ATSAIC: Assistant to the Special Agent in Charge</li>
<li>Driver Agent: Secret Service driver agents operated through their own command chain. Driver agents were typically recruited from the uniformed <a href="/wiki/White_House_Police_Force" title="White House Police Force">White House Police Force</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidential_motorcade_route">Presidential motorcade route</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Presidential motorcade route">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The motorcade route schedule was as follows: left turn from the south end of Love Field to West Mockingbird Lane, right on Lemmon Ave., right at the "Y" on Turtle Creek Blvd, straight on Cedar Springs Rd, left on North Harwood St, right on Main St, right on Houston St, sharp left on Elm St, through Triple Underpass, right turn up ramp to North Stemmons Freeway, to Dallas Trade Mart at 2100 North Stemmons. This same exact route cannot be driven today; there is a "No right turn" sign on the corner of Main and Houston Streets as well as some highway progressions in other areas.
</p><p>The presidential motorcade began its route without incident, stopping twice so President Kennedy could shake hands with some Catholic nuns, then some school children.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dealey-plaza-annotated.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Dealey-plaza-annotated.png/290px-Dealey-plaza-annotated.png" decoding="async" width="290" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Dealey-plaza-annotated.png/435px-Dealey-plaza-annotated.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Dealey-plaza-annotated.png/580px-Dealey-plaza-annotated.png 2x" data-file-width="592" data-file-height="546" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dealey-plaza-annotated.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The route taken by the motorcade within Dealey Plaza. North is towards the almost direct-left</div></div></div>
<p>At 12:29&#160;p.m. CST, the presidential limousine entered <a href="/wiki/Dealey_Plaza" title="Dealey Plaza">Dealey Plaza</a> after a 90-degree right turn from Main Street onto Houston Street. Over two dozen known and unknown amateur and professional still and motion-picture photographers captured the last living images of President Kennedy.
</p><p>Just before 12:30&#160;p.m. CST, President Kennedy was riding on Houston Street and slowly approached the <a href="/wiki/Texas_School_Book_Depository" title="Texas School Book Depository">Texas School Book Depository</a> head-on.
</p>
<h3><span id="12:30_p.m._.28CST.29:_Shots_are_fired"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="12:30_p.m._(CST):_Shots_are_fired">12:30 p.m. (CST): Shots are fired</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 12:30 p.m. (CST): Shots are fired">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to witnesses, the shooting occurred shortly after the limousine made the sharp left-hand turn from Houston onto Elm Street. Most of the witnesses recalled that the first shot was fired after the president had started waving with his right hand. Several onlookers recalled hearing three shots, with the second and third shots bunched distinctly much closer together than the first and second shots. Witnesses estimate that from three to eight shots were fired.  The <a href="/wiki/Zapruder_film" title="Zapruder film">Zapruder film</a> shows the President re-emerging in the footage after being temporarily hidden from view by the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_35E_(Texas)" title="Interstate 35E (Texas)">Stemmons Freeway</a> sign at Zapruder film frames 215 to 223; his mouth has already opened wide in an anguished expression by frame 225. He has already been impacted by a bullet, which hit him in the upper back and exited his throat, and his hands clench into fists. He then quickly raises his fists dramatically in front of his face and throat as he turns leftwards towards his wife. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secret_Service" title="United States Secret Service">Secret Service</a> Agent <a href="/wiki/Clint_Hill_(Secret_Service)" title="Clint Hill (Secret Service)">Clint Hill</a> testified that he heard one shot, then jumped off the running board of the Secret Service follow-up car directly behind Kennedy (Hill was filmed jumping off his follow-up car at the equivalent of Zapruder frame 308; about a quarter of a second before the president's head exploded at frame 313). Hill then rapidly ran towards the Presidential limo and then another shot hit Kennedy in the head, cracking open the right side of his skull. As the limousine began speeding up, Mrs. Kennedy was heard to scream<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> and she climbed out of the back seat onto the rear of the limo. At the same time, Hill managed to climb aboard and hang onto the suddenly accelerating limo, and Mrs. Kennedy returned to the back seat. Hill then shielded her and the President. Both of the Connallys stated they heard Mrs. Kennedy say, "I have his brains in my hand!" The limo driver and police motorcycles turned on their sirens and raced at high speeds to <a href="/wiki/Parkland_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="Parkland Hospital">Parkland Hospital</a>, passing their intended destination of the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Trade_Mart" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas Trade Mart">Dallas Trade Mart</a> along the way, and arriving at about 12:38&#160;p.m. (CST).
</p><p>Governor Connally was also struck by the shots, and his wife pulled him closer to her. He suffered several severe wounds that he survived; a bullet entry wound in his upper right back located just behind his right armpit; four inches of his right, fifth chest rib was pulverised; a two-and-a-half inch sized chest exit wound; his right arm's wrist bone was fractured into seven pieces; and he had a bullet entry wound in his left inner thigh. Although there is controversy about exactly when he was wounded, analysts from both the <a href="/wiki/Warren_Commission" title="Warren Commission">Warren Commission</a> (1964) and House Select Committee on Assassinations (1979) believed that his wounds had been inflicted nearly simultaneously with President Kennedy's in their theories that the two men were struck by a single bullet. The Commission theorized both men were hit nearly simultaneously between Zapruder film frames 210 to 225, while the Committee theorized it happened at frame 190.
</p><p>Witness <a href="/wiki/James_Tague" title="James Tague">James Tague</a> was also injured by the shots when he received a superficial face wound. The Main Street south curb he had been standing 23.5 feet away from was struck by a bullet or bullet fragment that had no copper sheath, and a fragment of the concrete curb or a bullet fragment struck Tague on his right cheek. At Zapruder frame 313 Tague's head top was located 271 feet away from and 16.4 feet below President Kennedy's head top and the limousine's front windshield and its pushed nearly vertically straight-upwards sun visors were in between the president and the impacted curb point. The bullet or bullet fragment that struck the concrete curb was never found.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Immediate_aftermath">Immediate aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Immediate aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lee_Harvey_Oswald">Lee Harvey Oswald</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Lee Harvey Oswald">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dallas Patrolman Marion L. Baker had been assigned to serve as a motorcycle escort for the motorcade, and he was riding just behind the camera cars. He testified that the first shot he could hear was fired after he turned from Main St. onto Houston St. and had traveled approximately 60 to 80 feet along Houston as he approached the Houston and Elm streets intersection. Baker stated that he recognized the first shot he could hear as the report of a high-powered rifle and that he thought the shots had originated from the building "either right in front of me [the Depository] or the one across to the right of it" [the Dallas Textile Building (DalTex)]. He also said that he noticed pigeons take flight up from the roof of the depository building and start flying around. Baker then quickly drove to the corner of Houston and Elm St., parked his motorcycle, then looked westward into the aftermath of persons screaming, running and laying on the ground. He then listened to Chief Curry's radio broadcast saying, "Get some men up on that railroad track".
</p><p>Baker then ran to the entrance of the Texas School Book Depository, entered the building with his gun drawn, and led by building superintendent Roy Truly, made his way to the far northwest corner of the first floor. From there, Baker and Truly started yelling for someone to send an elevator down from a higher floor. When there was no response, the two men began climbing the stairs, with Truly in the lead. Approximately 90 seconds after the shots rang out, Baker stepped out onto the second floor and a movement towards the lunchroom vestibule across from the stairs caught his attention. Baker confronted Oswald at gunpoint. He let Oswald pass after Truly identified him as an employee. According to Baker, Oswald did not appear to be nervous or out of breath.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Truly said that Oswald appeared "startled" when Baker aimed his gun at him.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> According to the Warren Commission, Oswald was next seen by a secretary as he crossed through the second-floor business office carrying a soda bottle.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> He left the Texas School Book Depository through its front door at approximately 12:33&#160;p.m.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Warren Commission theorized that Oswald had traveled from the sixth-floor easternmost window, and hid an 8-pound, Italian-made 1940 <a href="/wiki/Carcano" title="Carcano">Carcano</a>, 6.5-millimeter rifle equipped with a four-power scope along the way. The rifle was reportedly discovered near the sixth-floor northwest corner by a Dallas police detective at 1:22&#160;p.m., having been placed down between stacks of boxes, balanced upright on the lowest edges of its barrel and wooden stock. After being discovered, the rifle was photographed before being touched and was filmed while it was being inspected by the police crime lab supervisor.
</p><p>Estimates of when the depository building was sealed off by police range from 12:33 to 12:50&#160;p.m.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The Dealey Plaza immediate area streets and blocks were never sealed-off, and nine minutes after the assassination, photographs show that vehicles were still driving unhampered down Elm Street, through the crime scene kill zone.
</p><p>After leaving the depository, Oswald walked seven blocks before boarding a bus. When the bus got stuck in traffic, he got off, walked to a nearby bus station, entered a taxi, took it several blocks past his rooming house, and then walked back to the rooming house. He arrived at his rooming house at 1026 North Beckley Ave. at around 1:00&#160;p.m. According to his housekeeper Earlene Roberts, he left three or four minutes later. She last saw him standing and waiting at a bus stop outside the rooming house.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At 1:15 p.m, Oswald shot and killed Dallas police officer <a href="/wiki/J._D._Tippit" title="J. D. Tippit">J. D. Tippit</a> near the intersection of 10th St. and Patton Ave.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> This was 0.86 mile from Oswald's rooming house. Thirteen people witnessed Oswald shooting Tippit or fleeing the immediate scene.<sup id="cite_ref-TippitMurder_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TippitMurder-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bugliosi_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bugliosi-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> By that evening, five of the witnesses had identified him in police lineups, and a sixth identified him the following day. Four others subsequently identified Oswald from a photograph.<sup id="cite_ref-TippitMurder_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TippitMurder-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bugliosi_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bugliosi-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After killing Tippit, Oswald was seen traveling on foot toward the Texas Theater on West Jefferson Blvd.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> About 1:35&#160;p.m. Johnny Calvin Brewer, who worked as a manager at Hardy's Shoe Store in the same block as the Texas Theater on Jefferson Blvd. saw Oswald turning his face away from the street and duck into the entranceway of the shoe store as Dallas squad cars drove up the street with sirens on. When Oswald left the store, Brewer followed Oswald and watched him go into the Texas Theater movie house without paying while ticket attendant Julie Postal was distracted. Brewer notified Postal, who in turn informed the Dallas Police at 1:40&#160;p.m.
</p><p>Almost two dozen policemen, sheriffs, and detectives in several patrol cars arrived at Texas Theater because they believed Tippit's killer was inside. When an arrest attempt was made at 1:50&#160;p.m. inside the theater, Oswald resisted arrest and, according to the police, attempted to shoot a patrolman after yelling once, "Well, it's all over now!" then punching a patrolman.<sup id="cite_ref-NBCNews-Page32_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBCNews-Page32-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="President_Kennedy">President Kennedy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Timeline_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_assassination&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: President Kennedy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
